{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Bvmi1UU1Cq1UerH7Jj7eYz","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_011TX5WazoZXdfS4khGF2r93","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)\n\n## Overview\n\nThis guide documents the changes to the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter when upgrading from **v1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **v1.31.0 (July 2024)**. The ext_proc filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses by implementing a gRPC bidirectional stream protocol.\n\nThe v1.31 release introduces improvements for route cache management and observability mode features, along with behavioral changes for timeout error handling. Most configurations will work without modification, but recommended updates and new features should be evaluated.\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout Error Status Code Change\n\n**Impact Level:** HIGH - Affects downstream client behavior\n\n#### Change Description\nIn v1.30, when a message timeout occurred in the external processor, Envoy returned a **`500 Internal Server Error`** status code to downstream clients.\n\nIn v1.31, timeout errors now return **`504 Gateway Timeout`** status code.\n\n#### Motivation\nThe `504 Gateway Timeout` status code is more semantically correct for external service timeouts, allowing clients to distinguish between Envoy-internal errors (500) and upstream/external service timeouts (504). This enables better error handling and retry logic in downstream systems.\n\n#### Migration Impact\n- **Downstream clients** may handle 504 responses differently than 500 responses\n- **Error handling code** that checks for HTTP status 500 in the context of ext_proc timeouts should be updated\n- **Monitoring and alerting** based on status codes should be reviewed\n\n#### Example\n**v1.30 Behavior:**\n```\nClient Request → Envoy → External Processor (timeout)\n← HTTP 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**v1.31 Behavior:**\n```\nClient Request → Envoy → External Processor (timeout)\n← HTTP 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n#### Mitigation\n- Update downstream error handling to expect 504 responses\n- Review monitoring dashboards and alert thresholds\n- Test client retry logic with the new status code\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Deprecation Level:** MEDIUM - Field still functional but superseded\n\n#### What's Deprecated\nThe boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` in the `ExternalProcessor` message is now deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum field.\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `disable_clear_route_cache`\n- **Field Number:** 11\n- **Type:** `bool`\n- **Status:** Deprecated (marked with UDPA field migration annotation)\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n#### Why It's Deprecated\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field provides limited control with only two options:\n- `false` (default): Clear route cache when external processor requests it\n- `true`: Never clear route cache\n\nThe new `route_cache_action` enum provides three explicit options for finer control over route cache behavior, making configurations more explicit and readable.\n\n#### Backward Compatibility Behavior\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` field remains functional in v1.31:\n- If set to `true`, it is automatically converted to `route_cache_action = RETAIN`\n- If both fields are set to non-default values, **validation will fail**\n\n#### Code Reference\nSee `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:213-221` for the automatic conversion logic:\n\n```cpp\nif (config.disable_clear_route_cache()) {\n  route_cache_action_ = envoy::extensions::filters::http::ext_proc::v3::ExternalProcessor::RETAIN;\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\nReplace usage of `disable_clear_route_cache` with the equivalent `route_cache_action` value:\n\n| Old Setting | New Setting |\n|------------|------------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n\n**v1.30 Configuration:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration (Recommended):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Control\n\n**Feature Level:** MEDIUM - Enhanced configuration control\n\n#### What's New\nA new `route_cache_action` enum field provides three explicit options for controlling route cache behavior in response to external processor responses.\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `route_cache_action`\n- **Field Number:** 18\n- **Type:** `RouteCacheAction` enum\n- **Default Value:** `DEFAULT`\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto:105-120, 257-258`\n\n#### RouteCacheAction Enum Values\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default behavior: clear cache only when ext_proc response has clear_route_cache set\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache (equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true)\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior Description\n\nThe route cache action is evaluated in `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc:422-462`:\n\n| Action | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| **DEFAULT** | Route cache is cleared **only if** the external processor response includes `clear_route_cache: true`. This is the default behavior and maintains backward compatibility with v1.30. |\n| **CLEAR** | Route cache is **always cleared** when an external processor responds to request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. |\n| **RETAIN** | Route cache is **never cleared**, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` flag in the external processor response. Equivalent to setting `disable_clear_route_cache: true`. |\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n**Use `DEFAULT`:**\n- Let the external processor control route cache clearing\n- Most flexible option for processors that make dynamic decisions\n- External processor sets `clear_route_cache: true` in response when needed\n\n**Use `CLEAR`:**\n- Always invalidate routes after external processor processing\n- Useful when the external processor might modify headers that affect routing\n- Ensures routes are recomputed for every request\n- Conservative approach with potential performance implications\n\n**Use `RETAIN`:**\n- Prevent route cache invalidation completely\n- Useful when you're confident the external processor won't affect routing\n- Better performance by avoiding route recomputation\n- External processor's `clear_route_cache` flag is ignored\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Default behavior (backward compatible with v1.30)**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Example 2: Always clear route cache after ext_proc processing**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Example 3: Never clear route cache**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\nThe route cache action is used in the `clearRouteCache()` method:\n\n```cpp\nswitch (filter_.config().routeCacheAction()) {\n  case ExternalProcessor::DEFAULT:\n    if (response_clear_route_cache) {\n      decoder_callbacks_->downstreamCallbacks()->clearRouteCache();\n    }\n    break;\n  case ExternalProcessor::CLEAR:\n    decoder_callbacks_->downstreamCallbacks()->clearRouteCache();\n    break;\n  case ExternalProcessor::RETAIN:\n    if (response_clear_route_cache) {\n      filter_.stats().clear_route_cache_disabled_.inc();\n    }\n    break;\n}\n```\n\n#### Statistics\nWhen `RETAIN` is used and the external processor requests cache clearing:\n- Statistic `clear_route_cache_disabled_` is incremented\n- A debug log message is emitted: \"NOT clearing route cache, it is disabled by the filter config\"\n\n---\n\n### 2. Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Feature Level:** MEDIUM - Observability mode enhancement\n\n#### What's New\nA new `deferred_close_timeout` field specifies how long Envoy will wait before forcibly closing gRPC streams that are being deferred (kept open beyond the normal request/response lifecycle).\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `deferred_close_timeout`\n- **Field Number:** 19\n- **Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n- **Default Value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto:260-265`\n\n#### Purpose and Context\n\nIn **observability mode** (when `observability_mode: true`), the ext_proc filter operates in a \"send and go\" mode where:\n\n1. Envoy sends HTTP request/response data to the external processor **without waiting for a response**\n2. The external processor stream may remain open longer than the normal client-to-backend stream lifetime\n3. Without a timeout, streams could remain open indefinitely, consuming resources\n\nThe `deferred_close_timeout` ensures that these deferred streams are eventually closed:\n\n```cpp\n// In ext_proc.h:148-151\ninline constexpr uint32_t DEFAULT_DEFERRED_CLOSE_TIMEOUT_MS = 5000;\n\n// In ext_proc.h:385-389\nvoid Filter::deferredCloseStream() {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Calling deferred close on stream\");\n  config_->threadLocalStreamManager().deferredErase(decoder_callbacks_->streamId(),\n                                                    filter_callbacks_->dispatcher());\n}\n```\n\n#### When It's Used\n\nThe deferred close timeout is **only used in observability mode**:\n\n```cpp\nif (config_->observabilityMode()) {\n  // In observability mode where the main stream processing and side stream processing are\n  // asynchronous, it is possible that filter instance is destroyed before the side stream request\n  // arrives at ext_proc server. In order to prevent the data loss in this case, side stream\n  // closure is deferred upon filter destruction with a timer.\n  deferredCloseStream();\n}\n```\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Using default timeout (5 seconds):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  # deferred_close_timeout defaults to 5000ms\n```\n\n**Custom timeout (10 seconds):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s\n```\n\n**Short timeout (1 second, for tight resource constraints):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 1s\n```\n\n#### Tuning Guidance\n\n**Increase the timeout if:**\n- Your external processor is experiencing latency spikes\n- You observe frequent \"deferred close timeout exceeded\" errors in logs\n- You want to ensure all observability data is fully transmitted\n\n**Decrease the timeout if:**\n- You're concerned about resource consumption\n- Your external processor responds quickly\n- You have many concurrent streams and want faster cleanup\n\n---\n\n### 3. Observability Mode (as improved feature)\n\n**Feature Level:** HIGH - Enhanced monitoring capabilities\n\n#### Overview\nObservability mode (first introduced in v1.31) allows the ext_proc filter to operate in a \"send and go\" mode where data is sent to the external processor without waiting for responses. This mode is useful for non-invasive monitoring and observability.\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n1. **Fire-and-forget semantics:** Envoy sends data but doesn't wait for processor responses\n2. **Only STREAMED body mode supported:** Other body processing modes are ignored\n3. **No message timeout restrictions:** The `message_timeout` configuration doesn't apply\n4. **Stream can still be closed:** External processor can still close the stream to signal completion\n\n#### Configuration\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Timeout for deferred stream closure\n```\n\n#### Deprecation Note\nThe `async_mode` field in `ExtProcOverrides` is deprecated and superseded by observability mode. While `async_mode` is still present in the proto definition, it is marked with `[#not-implemented-hide:]` and is not fully implemented.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Inventory Current Configurations\n\nIdentify all Envoy configurations using the ext_proc filter:\n\n```bash\n# Search for ext_proc configurations\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\\|envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\" *.yaml *.yml\n```\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate Route Cache Behavior\n\nFor each ext_proc filter configuration, determine the current route cache behavior:\n\n1. **If `disable_clear_route_cache` is not set or is `false`:**\n   - Current behavior: DEFAULT (clear cache only when processor requests it)\n   - Action: No change needed, or add explicit `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n2. **If `disable_clear_route_cache` is `true`:**\n   - Current behavior: RETAIN (never clear cache)\n   - Action: Replace with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n### Step 3: Update Configurations\n\nReplace deprecated `disable_clear_route_cache` usage with `route_cache_action`:\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Step 4: Evaluate New Features\n\nConsider adopting new features if beneficial:\n\n1. **Route Cache Action (CLEAR mode):**\n   - If you need aggressive route cache invalidation\n   - When external processor modifies routing-related headers\n\n2. **Observability Mode:**\n   - If you need non-invasive monitoring\n   - For collecting telemetry without affecting request processing\n   - Set appropriate `deferred_close_timeout` (default 5s is usually fine)\n\n### Step 5: Test Error Handling\n\nTest that downstream systems handle `504 Gateway Timeout` correctly:\n\n1. Simulate ext_proc timeout scenarios\n2. Verify client retry logic works with 504 responses\n3. Check monitoring and alerting systems\n4. Test load balancers and proxies in front of Envoy\n\n### Step 6: Monitor and Validate\n\nAfter migration:\n\n1. **Monitor ext_proc statistics:**\n   ```\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_started\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_closed\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_failed\n   envoy_ext_proc_message_timeouts\n   envoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_disabled\n   envoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_ignored\n   ```\n\n2. **Check logs for deprecation warnings:**\n   - Debug logs should show route cache actions being applied\n   - No validation errors about conflicting cache settings\n\n3. **Validate behavior:**\n   - Route caching works as expected\n   - Timeout responses have correct status codes\n   - Observability data is collected (if using observability mode)\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Unit Testing\n\nTest your configuration changes:\n\n```yaml\n# Test case: route_cache_action DEFAULT\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n# Expected: External processor controls cache clearing\n\n# Test case: route_cache_action CLEAR\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n# Expected: Route cache always cleared\n\n# Test case: route_cache_action RETAIN\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n# Expected: Route cache never cleared\n```\n\n### 2. Integration Testing\n\nTest with your actual external processor:\n\n1. **Timeout scenarios:**\n   - Simulate ext_proc service delay\n   - Verify clients receive 504 responses (not 500)\n   - Check retry logic works correctly\n\n2. **Route cache scenarios:**\n   - External processor modifies routing headers\n   - Verify cache is invalidated according to `route_cache_action`\n   - Test both request-specific and global route changes\n\n3. **Observability mode (if using):**\n   - Enable observability mode\n   - Verify data is sent without waiting for responses\n   - Check `deferred_close_timeout` is appropriate for your system\n\n### 3. Performance Testing\n\nValidate performance impact:\n\n1. **Route cache efficiency:**\n   - Compare cache hit rates with DEFAULT vs. CLEAR actions\n   - CLEAR mode may reduce cache hit rate if processor modifies headers\n\n2. **Resource usage:**\n   - Monitor stream creation/destruction rates\n   - Verify deferred close timeouts prevent resource leaks\n   - Check memory usage under load\n\n### 4. Load Testing\n\nRun load tests with v1.31:\n\n```bash\n# Example: Load test with timeout scenarios\n# - 95% normal requests\n# - 5% requests that timeout\n# Verify 504 responses and downstream handling\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31:\n\n### Quick Rollback\n\n1. **Revert to v1.30:**\n   - Restore previous Envoy binary/container image\n   - Configurations using `route_cache_action` will be converted to `disable_clear_route_cache` automatically\n   - Restart Envoy\n\n2. **Configuration changes (if needed):**\n   - If you updated configs to use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`, change back to `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n   - Other changes can remain as they're backward compatible\n\n### Specific Issues and Solutions\n\n**Issue: 504 responses breaking downstream clients**\n- **Cause:** Clients don't expect 504 status from ext_proc timeouts\n- **Solution:**\n  - Increase `message_timeout` in ext_proc config (default 200ms)\n  - Improve external processor performance\n  - Update client error handling to expect 504\n\n**Issue: Validation error about conflicting cache settings**\n- **Cause:** Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` are set to non-default values\n- **Solution:** Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` and only use `route_cache_action`\n\n**Issue: Route cache not being cleared when expected**\n- **Cause:** Configuration uses `route_cache_action: RETAIN` or `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` without processor requesting it\n- **Solution:**\n  - Change to `route_cache_action: CLEAR` if always need to clear\n  - Verify external processor is sending `clear_route_cache: true` in DEFAULT mode\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### 1. Conflict Between disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action\n\n**Problem:** Setting both fields to non-default values causes a validation error:\n```\n\"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n```\n\n**Solution:** Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` entirely and use only `route_cache_action`.\n\n### 2. Unexpected 504 Responses\n\n**Problem:** Downstream systems receive 504 responses instead of expected 500 responses.\n\n**Solution:**\n- Update error handling code to expect 504\n- Consider increasing `message_timeout` if external processor is slow\n- Review external processor performance\n\n### 3. Route Cache Behavior Changes\n\n**Problem:** Route caching behavior differs from v1.30 after migration.\n\n**Root Cause:** Forgetting to migrate `disable_clear_route_cache: true` to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n**Solution:** Ensure every instance of `disable_clear_route_cache` is replaced with appropriate `route_cache_action` value.\n\n### 4. Observability Mode Resource Issues\n\n**Problem:** gRPC streams to external processor stay open too long, consuming resources.\n\n**Cause:** `deferred_close_timeout` too large for your environment.\n\n**Solution:** Tune `deferred_close_timeout` to appropriate value (e.g., 2-5 seconds).\n\n---\n\n## Reference Materials\n\n### Proto Definitions\n- **v1.31 ext_proc.proto:** The ext_proc filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses by implementing a gRPC bidirectional stream protocol.\n\nThe v1.31 release introduces improvements for route cache management and observability mode features, along with behavioral changes for timeout error handling. Most configurations will work without modification, but recommended updates and new features should be evaluated.\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout Error Status Code Change\n\n**Impact Level:** HIGH - Affects downstream client behavior\n\n#### Change Description\nIn v1.30, when a message timeout occurred in the external processor, Envoy returned a **`500 Internal Server Error`** status code to downstream clients.\n\nIn v1.31, timeout errors now return **`504 Gateway Timeout`** status code.\n\n#### Motivation\nThe `504 Gateway Timeout` status code is more semantically correct for external service timeouts, allowing clients to distinguish between Envoy-internal errors (500) and upstream/external service timeouts (504). This enables better error handling and retry logic in downstream systems.\n\n#### Migration Impact\n- **Downstream clients** may handle 504 responses differently than 500 responses\n- **Error handling code** that checks for HTTP status 500 in the context of ext_proc timeouts should be updated\n- **Monitoring and alerting** based on status codes should be reviewed\n\n#### Example\n**v1.30 Behavior:**\n```\nClient Request → Envoy → External Processor (timeout)\n← HTTP 500 Internal Server Error\n```\n\n**v1.31 Behavior:**\n```\nClient Request → Envoy → External Processor (timeout)\n← HTTP 504 Gateway Timeout\n```\n\n#### Mitigation\n- Update downstream error handling to expect 504 responses\n- Review monitoring dashboards and alert thresholds\n- Test client retry logic with the new status code\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` Field\n\n**Deprecation Level:** MEDIUM - Field still functional but superseded\n\n#### What's Deprecated\nThe boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` in the `ExternalProcessor` message is now deprecated in favor of the new `route_cache_action` enum field.\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `disable_clear_route_cache`\n- **Field Number:** 11\n- **Type:** `bool`\n- **Status:** Deprecated (marked with UDPA field migration annotation)\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n#### Why It's Deprecated\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean field provides limited control with only two options:\n- `false` (default): Clear route cache when external processor requests it\n- `true`: Never clear route cache\n\nThe new `route_cache_action` enum provides three explicit options for finer control over route cache behavior, making configurations more explicit and readable.\n\n#### Backward Compatibility Behavior\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache` field remains functional in v1.31:\n- If set to `true`, it is automatically converted to `route_cache_action = RETAIN`\n- If both fields are set to non-default values, **validation will fail**\n\n#### Code Reference\nSee `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc:213-221` for the automatic conversion logic:\n\n```cpp\nif (config.disable_clear_route_cache()) {\n  route_cache_action_ = envoy::extensions::filters::http::ext_proc::v3::ExternalProcessor::RETAIN;\n}\n```\n\n#### Migration Path\nReplace usage of `disable_clear_route_cache` with the equivalent `route_cache_action` value:\n\n| Old Setting | New Setting |\n|------------|------------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` |\n\n**v1.30 Configuration:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**v1.31 Configuration (Recommended):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. Route Cache Action Control\n\n**Feature Level:** MEDIUM - Enhanced configuration control\n\n#### What's New\nA new `route_cache_action` enum field provides three explicit options for controlling route cache behavior in response to external processor responses.\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `route_cache_action`\n- **Field Number:** 18\n- **Type:** `RouteCacheAction` enum\n- **Default Value:** `DEFAULT`\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto:105-120, 257-258`\n\n#### RouteCacheAction Enum Values\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default behavior: clear cache only when ext_proc response has clear_route_cache set\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache regardless of ext_proc response\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache (equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache: true)\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n```\n\n#### Behavior Description\n\nThe route cache action is evaluated in `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc:422-462`:\n\n| Action | Behavior |\n|--------|----------|\n| **DEFAULT** | Route cache is cleared **only if** the external processor response includes `clear_route_cache: true`. This is the default behavior and maintains backward compatibility with v1.30. |\n| **CLEAR** | Route cache is **always cleared** when an external processor responds to request headers, regardless of the `clear_route_cache` field in the response. |\n| **RETAIN** | Route cache is **never cleared**, ignoring any `clear_route_cache` flag in the external processor response. Equivalent to setting `disable_clear_route_cache: true`. |\n\n#### Use Cases\n\n**Use `DEFAULT`:**\n- Let the external processor control route cache clearing\n- Most flexible option for processors that make dynamic decisions\n- External processor sets `clear_route_cache: true` in response when needed\n\n**Use `CLEAR`:**\n- Always invalidate routes after external processor processing\n- Useful when the external processor might modify headers that affect routing\n- Ensures routes are recomputed for every request\n- Conservative approach with potential performance implications\n\n**Use `RETAIN`:**\n- Prevent route cache invalidation completely\n- Useful when you're confident the external processor won't affect routing\n- Better performance by avoiding route recomputation\n- External processor's `clear_route_cache` flag is ignored\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Example 1: Default behavior (backward compatible with v1.30)**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n```\n\n**Example 2: Always clear route cache after ext_proc processing**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**Example 3: Never clear route cache**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n#### Implementation Details\n\nThe route cache action is used in the `clearRouteCache()` method:\n\n```cpp\nswitch (filter_.config().routeCacheAction()) {\n  case ExternalProcessor::DEFAULT:\n    if (response_clear_route_cache) {\n      decoder_callbacks_->downstreamCallbacks()->clearRouteCache();\n    }\n    break;\n  case ExternalProcessor::CLEAR:\n    decoder_callbacks_->downstreamCallbacks()->clearRouteCache();\n    break;\n  case ExternalProcessor::RETAIN:\n    if (response_clear_route_cache) {\n      filter_.stats().clear_route_cache_disabled_.inc();\n    }\n    break;\n}\n```\n\n#### Statistics\nWhen `RETAIN` is used and the external processor requests cache clearing:\n- Statistic `clear_route_cache_disabled_` is incremented\n- A debug log message is emitted: \"NOT clearing route cache, it is disabled by the filter config\"\n\n---\n\n### 2. Deferred Stream Closure Timeout\n\n**Feature Level:** MEDIUM - Observability mode enhancement\n\n#### What's New\nA new `deferred_close_timeout` field specifies how long Envoy will wait before forcibly closing gRPC streams that are being deferred (kept open beyond the normal request/response lifecycle).\n\n**Proto Field Details:**\n- **Field Name:** `deferred_close_timeout`\n- **Field Number:** 19\n- **Type:** `google.protobuf.Duration`\n- **Default Value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto:260-265`\n\n#### Purpose and Context\n\nIn **observability mode** (when `observability_mode: true`), the ext_proc filter operates in a \"send and go\" mode where:\n\n1. Envoy sends HTTP request/response data to the external processor **without waiting for a response**\n2. The external processor stream may remain open longer than the normal client-to-backend stream lifetime\n3. Without a timeout, streams could remain open indefinitely, consuming resources\n\nThe `deferred_close_timeout` ensures that these deferred streams are eventually closed:\n\n```cpp\n// In ext_proc.h:148-151\ninline constexpr uint32_t DEFAULT_DEFERRED_CLOSE_TIMEOUT_MS = 5000;\n\n// In ext_proc.h:385-389\nvoid Filter::deferredCloseStream() {\n  ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"Calling deferred close on stream\");\n  config_->threadLocalStreamManager().deferredErase(decoder_callbacks_->streamId(),\n                                                    filter_callbacks_->dispatcher());\n}\n```\n\n#### When It's Used\n\nThe deferred close timeout is **only used in observability mode**:\n\n```cpp\nif (config_->observabilityMode()) {\n  // In observability mode where the main stream processing and side stream processing are\n  // asynchronous, it is possible that filter instance is destroyed before the side stream request\n  // arrives at ext_proc server. In order to prevent the data loss in this case, side stream\n  // closure is deferred upon filter destruction with a timer.\n  deferredCloseStream();\n}\n```\n\n#### Configuration Examples\n\n**Using default timeout (5 seconds):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  # deferred_close_timeout defaults to 5000ms\n```\n\n**Custom timeout (10 seconds):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s\n```\n\n**Short timeout (1 second, for tight resource constraints):**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 1s\n```\n\n#### Tuning Guidance\n\n**Increase the timeout if:**\n- Your external processor is experiencing latency spikes\n- You observe frequent \"deferred close timeout exceeded\" errors in logs\n- You want to ensure all observability data is fully transmitted\n\n**Decrease the timeout if:**\n- You're concerned about resource consumption\n- Your external processor responds quickly\n- You have many concurrent streams and want faster cleanup\n\n---\n\n### 3. Observability Mode (as improved feature)\n\n**Feature Level:** HIGH - Enhanced monitoring capabilities\n\n#### Overview\nObservability mode (first introduced in v1.31) allows the ext_proc filter to operate in a \"send and go\" mode where data is sent to the external processor without waiting for responses. This mode is useful for non-invasive monitoring and observability.\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n1. **Fire-and-forget semantics:** Envoy sends data but doesn't wait for processor responses\n2. **Only STREAMED body mode supported:** Other body processing modes are ignored\n3. **No message timeout restrictions:** The `message_timeout` configuration doesn't apply\n4. **Stream can still be closed:** External processor can still close the stream to signal completion\n\n#### Configuration\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s  # Timeout for deferred stream closure\n```\n\n#### Deprecation Note\nThe `async_mode` field in `ExtProcOverrides` is deprecated and superseded by observability mode. While `async_mode` is still present in the proto definition, it is marked with `[#not-implemented-hide:]` and is not fully implemented.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Inventory Current Configurations\n\nIdentify all Envoy configurations using the ext_proc filter:\n\n```bash\n# Search for ext_proc configurations\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\\|envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\" *.yaml *.yml\n```\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate Route Cache Behavior\n\nFor each ext_proc filter configuration, determine the current route cache behavior:\n\n1. **If `disable_clear_route_cache` is not set or is `false`:**\n   - Current behavior: DEFAULT (clear cache only when processor requests it)\n   - Action: No change needed, or add explicit `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n2. **If `disable_clear_route_cache` is `true`:**\n   - Current behavior: RETAIN (never clear cache)\n   - Action: Replace with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n### Step 3: Update Configurations\n\nReplace deprecated `disable_clear_route_cache` usage with `route_cache_action`:\n\n**Before (v1.30):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\n**After (v1.31):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Step 4: Evaluate New Features\n\nConsider adopting new features if beneficial:\n\n1. **Route Cache Action (CLEAR mode):**\n   - If you need aggressive route cache invalidation\n   - When external processor modifies routing-related headers\n\n2. **Observability Mode:**\n   - If you need non-invasive monitoring\n   - For collecting telemetry without affecting request processing\n   - Set appropriate `deferred_close_timeout` (default 5s is usually fine)\n\n### Step 5: Test Error Handling\n\nTest that downstream systems handle `504 Gateway Timeout` correctly:\n\n1. Simulate ext_proc timeout scenarios\n2. Verify client retry logic works with 504 responses\n3. Check monitoring and alerting systems\n4. Test load balancers and proxies in front of Envoy\n\n### Step 6: Monitor and Validate\n\nAfter migration:\n\n1. **Monitor ext_proc statistics:**\n   ```\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_started\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_closed\n   envoy_ext_proc_streams_failed\n   envoy_ext_proc_message_timeouts\n   envoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_disabled\n   envoy_ext_proc_clear_route_cache_ignored\n   ```\n\n2. **Check logs for deprecation warnings:**\n   - Debug logs should show route cache actions being applied\n   - No validation errors about conflicting cache settings\n\n3. **Validate behavior:**\n   - Route caching works as expected\n   - Timeout responses have correct status codes\n   - Observability data is collected (if using observability mode)\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### 1. Unit Testing\n\nTest your configuration changes:\n\n```yaml\n# Test case: route_cache_action DEFAULT\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT\n# Expected: External processor controls cache clearing\n\n# Test case: route_cache_action CLEAR\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n# Expected: Route cache always cleared\n\n# Test case: route_cache_action RETAIN\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n# Expected: Route cache never cleared\n```\n\n### 2. Integration Testing\n\nTest with your actual external processor:\n\n1. **Timeout scenarios:**\n   - Simulate ext_proc service delay\n   - Verify clients receive 504 responses (not 500)\n   - Check retry logic works correctly\n\n2. **Route cache scenarios:**\n   - External processor modifies routing headers\n   - Verify cache is invalidated according to `route_cache_action`\n   - Test both request-specific and global route changes\n\n3. **Observability mode (if using):**\n   - Enable observability mode\n   - Verify data is sent without waiting for responses\n   - Check `deferred_close_timeout` is appropriate for your system\n\n### 3. Performance Testing\n\nValidate performance impact:\n\n1. **Route cache efficiency:**\n   - Compare cache hit rates with DEFAULT vs. CLEAR actions\n   - CLEAR mode may reduce cache hit rate if processor modifies headers\n\n2. **Resource usage:**\n   - Monitor stream creation/destruction rates\n   - Verify deferred close timeouts prevent resource leaks\n   - Check memory usage under load\n\n### 4. Load Testing\n\nRun load tests with v1.31:\n\n```bash\n# Example: Load test with timeout scenarios\n# - 95% normal requests\n# - 5% requests that timeout\n# Verify 504 responses and downstream handling\n```\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31:\n\n### Quick Rollback\n\n1. **Revert to v1.30:**\n   - Restore previous Envoy binary/container image\n   - Configurations using `route_cache_action` will be converted to `disable_clear_route_cache` automatically\n   - Restart Envoy\n\n2. **Configuration changes (if needed):**\n   - If you updated configs to use `route_cache_action: RETAIN`, change back to `disable_clear_route_cache: true`\n   - Other changes can remain as they're backward compatible\n\n### Specific Issues and Solutions\n\n**Issue: 504 responses breaking downstream clients**\n- **Cause:** Clients don't expect 504 status from ext_proc timeouts\n- **Solution:**\n  - Increase `message_timeout` in ext_proc config (default 200ms)\n  - Improve external processor performance\n  - Update client error handling to expect 504\n\n**Issue: Validation error about conflicting cache settings**\n- **Cause:** Both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` are set to non-default values\n- **Solution:** Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` and only use `route_cache_action`\n\n**Issue: Route cache not being cleared when expected**\n- **Cause:** Configuration uses `route_cache_action: RETAIN` or `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` without processor requesting it\n- **Solution:**\n  - Change to `route_cache_action: CLEAR` if always need to clear\n  - Verify external processor is sending `clear_route_cache: true` in DEFAULT mode\n\n---\n\n## Common Migration Pitfalls\n\n### 1. Conflict Between disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action\n\n**Problem:** Setting both fields to non-default values causes a validation error:\n```\n\"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n```\n\n**Solution:** Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` entirely and use only `route_cache_action`.\n\n### 2. Unexpected 504 Responses\n\n**Problem:** Downstream systems receive 504 responses instead of expected 500 responses.\n\n**Solution:**\n- Update error handling code to expect 504\n- Consider increasing `message_timeout` if external processor is slow\n- Review external processor performance\n\n### 3. Route Cache Behavior Changes\n\n**Problem:** Route caching behavior differs from v1.30 after migration.\n\n**Root Cause:** Forgetting to migrate `disable_clear_route_cache: true` to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`.\n\n**Solution:** Ensure every instance of `disable_clear_route_cache` is replaced with appropriate `route_cache_action` value.\n\n### 4. Observability Mode Resource Issues\n\n**Problem:** gRPC streams to external processor stay open too long, consuming resources.\n\n**Cause:** `deferred_close_timeout` too large for your environment.\n\n**Solution:** Tune `deferred_close_timeout` to appropriate value (e.g., 2-5 seconds).\n\n---\n\n## Reference Materials\n\n### Proto Definitions\n- **v1.31 ext_proc.proto:**
